<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e1d2993f-edb0-4e14-ab5e-e26f8275d6e6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

When Cécile de Troyes is kidnapped and taken beneath the mountain, she realises that the trolls are relying on her to break the curse.<br /><br />Cécile has only one thing on her mind: escape. But the trolls are clever, fast, and inhumanly strong. She will have to bide her time…<br /><br />But the more time she spends with the trolls, the more she understands their plight. There is a rebellion brewing. And she just might be the one the trolls were looking for...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3480932371167115382"><b>Actual rating: 3.5</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Hmmm,” the King said, making a face. “I’m not sure this is what we bargained for, boy. We expected the girl to be attractive.”<br/><br/>If I hadn’t been so terrified, I would have been insulted.<br/><br/>“This is the one.”<br/><br/>“Are you certain?” the King asked from his perch on the throne. “She rather smells.”</i>
</blockquote>Mother of God. <b>A YA fantasy without insta-love. Without a love triangle. Without a Mary Sue who constantly complains about different she looks and how different she is from everyone else?!</b><br/><br/>It </span>
  <span id="freeText3480932371167115382" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 3.5</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Hmmm,” the King said, making a face. “I’m not sure this is what we bargained for, boy. We expected the girl to be attractive.”<br /><br />If I hadn’t been so terrified, I would have been insulted.<br /><br />“This is the one.”<br /><br />“Are you certain?” the King asked from his perch on the throne. “She rather smells.”</i>
</blockquote>Mother of God. <b>A YA fantasy without insta-love. Without a love triangle. Without a Mary Sue who constantly complains about different she looks and how different she is from everyone else?!</b><br /><br />It does exist.<br /><br />The premise is pretty terrible, because it screams SPECIAL DESTINED GIRL. It's not. Trust me, have patience with this book. Ignore the ugly cover. Ignore the Mary Sue blurb.<br /><br /><u>Summary</u>: Cécile de Troyes is a poor girl from a small village in the Hollows who has aspirations of being a singer. She's very, very good, but she's not exceptional. Cécile is returning to her village from a performance when she gets kidnapped and dragged underground. Literally. There was a bounty put on her head for a girl fitting her description.<blockquote>
  <i>"She foretold that when a prince of night bonded a daughter of the sun, the curse would be broken.”</i>
</blockquote>Her bounty is her weight in gold.<br /><br />Trolls do exist. They have a kingdom under the mountain, in a cave. For some reason they want Cécile. Why? Why the fuck do they want her in particular? What purpose do they have for her?<blockquote>
  <i>“She meets the criteria given to us by the foretelling. You do sing, don’t you?” the troll woman asked.<br /><br />“Yes,” I croaked, not knowing why it mattered. “What do you intend to do with me?”<br /><br />“Why, to bond you to our dear Tristan,” the troll said, smiling at me. “You are to be a princess of Trollus and mother of his children; and in doing so, you will set us all free.”</i>
</blockquote>Fuck that shit. Cécile has her own life. She loves her family. She wants nothing but to escape. Fuck being a princess in an underground city. THESE ARE TROLLS. They want to fucking MARRY her to a troll?!<blockquote>
  <i>Not all of them were deformed, but they were monsters still, every one of them. And I was to wed one. To be bedded by one. To bear its children. This wasn’t how it was supposed to go. I was supposed to be on my way to Trianon to get everything I had ever wanted. Now, not only had I lost everything – my family, my friends, my dreams – I had just been informed that what life I had left would be spent in an endless nightmare.</i>
</blockquote>The Prince Charming isn't exactly charming. He is rude, he is completely uninterested in her, and he thinks Cécile is an idiot.<blockquote>
  <i>“Ha ha,” Tristan snorted. “How dreadfully clever. And speaking of clever, is this to be your bid for escape?” He contemplated my clothing. “In a dressing gown and bare feet? Now tell me, if I go put on nightclothes and slippers, might I join you, or is this a solo adventure?”<br /><br />My eyes stung. “You think this is all exceedingly funny, don’t you? I’m nothing but a joke to you.”<br /><br />His brow creased in a frown. “If you’re a joke, it isn’t an especially humorous one.”</i>
</blockquote>He doesn't want her any more than she wants him. Tristan and Cécile are literally forced together for the sake of fulfilling a prophecy that is supposed to save the people of Trollus.<blockquote>
  <i>“You are the last person in the world I’d choose to marry,” I hissed.<br /><br />“I don’t entirely relish the idea myself,” Tristan said, “but sometimes we must do the unthinkable. Because you have no choice, just as I have no choice."</i>
</blockquote><b>Cécile is supposed to be the chosen one. The prophesied one whose marriage to Tristan will be the salvation of the people of Trollus.<br /><br />She fails.</b><blockquote>
  <i>We waited for what seemed like an eternity, then, abruptly, a collective groan of disappointment passed through the throng of trolls.<br /><br />“Did it work?” I asked, heartily wishing someone would explain what it was.<br /><br />“No,” Tristan said. “It didn’t.”</i>
</blockquote>Cécile is now a prisoner. A princess of the Trollus, but a prisoner just the same. She is a human, hated and reviled as an inferior creature among the trolls.<br /><br />Her story doesn't end there, because there are so many undercurrents lying beneath the mountain. An uprising is taking place. The prophecy might not be what it seems. There are traitors in the royal court, waiting for the chance to strike.<br /><br />Tristan himself is not the offhanded, ruthless prince he seems. He has secrets of his own. For their mutual survival, and for the cause, Cécile and Tristan must join forces, become reluctant allies, in order to free the people of Trollus.<blockquote>
  <i>“I will ignore you. Be cruel to you. And you must play along. Act sad and unhappy. Never give anyone a reason to think I’ve shown you a moment’s kindness or that I’ve confided in you in any way. And above all, never let anyone suspect that I care one way or another whether you live or die, beyond how it might impact me.”</i>
</blockquote>The fate of many rests upon their mission.<br /><br /><u>The Setting</u>: An cave underneath a mountain, and it is GLORIOUS. Carved masonry. Fantastic, magical underground gardens. Phantom, fairy lights. It is tremendously opulent, a stunningly beautiful jail to Cécile.<blockquote>
  <i>Fountains and statues graced every corner. In place of greenery stood gardens of glassworks sculpted into trees, bushes, and flowers. The delicate displays would not have lasted more than a month exposed to the elements above ground. Then again, hailstorms likely did not trouble Trollus.</i>
</blockquote>The history of the trolls were well explained, as was the myths surrounding the prophecy.<br /><br /><b>Oh, and those legends about trolls? They're just not true.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Almost too late did I see the beam of sunlight crossing his path.<br /><br />“No!” I gasped, throwing my weight into Tristan, knocking him down sideways into a narrow alleyway.<br /><br />I eyed the beam of sunlight that was still too close for comfort. “The sun.”<br /><br />“Everyone knows that trolls turn to stone in the sunlight,” I said.<br /><br />His astonishment faded and to my horror, he started to laugh. Reaching out one arm, he waggled his fingers in the sun. “Oh, the stories you humans come up with,” he gasped out, and my cheeks burned.</i>
</blockquote><u>Cécile</u>: The main character, one of the two narrators. <b>Cécile is the kind of heroine that I like</b>. She is NOT special. She never proclaims herself to be different. She is strong-willed, but never bitchy. She neither fall into insta-love or insta-lust nor does she allow her heart to overpower her sense of rationality.<br /><br />Cécile makes mistakes. She learns from them. She is not perfect. She admits her wrongs. Cécile is almost completely alone in a foreign land where she is reviled for the fact that she is an inferior human among trolls, and her persistance and attitude is just what I hope to see. She is strong, compassionate. She admits her faults, she recognizes when she fucks up.<blockquote>
  <i>“I’m sorry,” I whispered. But what good were my regrets? I’d ruined everything and still he’d come for me when I’d needed him the most. I’d told myself to make the most of my life in Trollus, but instead I’d made the least of it. The worst of it! Because of me, the only other person fighting for my freedom was dying.</i>
</blockquote><b>Cécile is properly angry at being kidnapped, but she does not waste her time moping.</b> She puts her time to good use, she devotes her time to a better purpose, and she overcomes her own prejudices of the trolls, as she comes to know them.<blockquote>
  <i>“Trolls,” I finally said, “are supposed to be ugly.”<br /><br />My thoughts turned to Marc, who was always kind to me when no one else was. “They aren’t ugly.” I bit my lip, trying to find the right words. “More like beautiful things that have had the misfortune of being broken.”</i>
</blockquote><u>Other Characters</u>: Very well done. <b>I love the depiction of other females in the books. There is no slut shaming, there is no debasement of other women.</b> There is bravery and sacrifice in other women's duties. *cheers*<br /><br />And let's just say there is a troll in the book named Marc, who won over my heart.<blockquote>
  <i>He was perhaps my brother’s age, and particularly handsome. The light of the orb reflected in his silvery grey eye as though the glow came from within. I’d never met anyone in my life with eyes like his.<br />The two sides of his face, so flawless on their own, were like halves of a fractured sculpture put back together askew.The lack of symmetry was more than unsettling – it was shocking, gruesome even. One eye higher than the other. One ear lower than the other. A mouth marred by a permanently sardonic twist.</i>
</blockquote>Be not fooled by his appearance. Marc has a heart of gold.<br /><br /><u>The Romance</u>: <b>AWESOME. AWESOME. No insta-love?! FUCK YEAH! YEAAAAAAH!</b><br /><br />Sorry, I get a little overexcited.<br /><br />Cécile and Tristan's relationship is so well-built. <b>Mistrust into alliance into friendship into love.</b><br /><br />Tristan is such a complicated character, his mission and purpose unwavering. He is prepared to make sacrifices of his life, his heart, for his people. He is a man on a mission, and I love it.<blockquote>
  <i>Almost every action I took or decision I made was designed to affect circumstances months, years, even decades down the road. I’d always thought it was the prudent way to live, but now I feared I would wake up one day an old man, with my past wasted and no future left to live.</i>
</blockquote>I absolutely adored how Tristan and Cécile come to trust and rely on one another. Their romance is one of sacrifice, because they are devoted to a cause higher than their own. If you love someone, you have to let them go.<blockquote>
  <i>“Under the sun, with your family. That’s where you belong.”</i>
</blockquote>It was beautiful seeing them love one another while knowing they come from two different worlds.<br /><br />Trolls cannot lie by nature. They are bound to their words. Humans are not so.<blockquote>
  <i>“Why?” I slammed my fists down on the table. “Why can’t you believe me? Why don’t you trust me?”<br /><br />“Because you’re human, Cécile. You can lie, even to yourself.”</i>
</blockquote>They have a lot of miscommunication, a lot of mistrust. There is a lot of difficulty in their relationship, because there are people who will use their love for each other against them. Danger and sacrifice fills their romance.<blockquote>
  <i>“Tell me you’ll grow strong again. That you’ll gallop on horseback through summer meadows. Dance in spring rains and let snowflakes melt on your tongue in winter. That you’ll travel wherever the wind takes you. Promise me."</i>
</blockquote>This book's major fault is that it is far too long. Much like my review ^_^<br /><br /><i>Quotes taken from an uncorrected galley subject to change in the final edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3480932371167115382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_821598672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/821598672" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/821598672?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer821598672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4968762233296554457"><b>"They were toying with me, like a pair of cats with a mouse... But I was no mouse."</b><br/><br/>I'm not sure how it happened. One minute I was reading this in bed and thinking "okay, just one more chapter and then I'll sleep", and the next minute there was sunlight coming in through my window! Oops.<br/><br/>So me and this 436-page book just spent a long night together and I feel a little frazzled and emotional - is this what they call <u>book withdrawal symptoms?</u> No, you're right, it's probably called sleep deprivation,</span>
  <span id="freeText4968762233296554457" style="display:none"><b>"They were toying with me, like a pair of cats with a mouse... But I was no mouse."</b><br><br>I'm not sure how it happened. One minute I was reading this in bed and thinking "okay, just one more chapter and then I'll sleep", and the next minute there was sunlight coming in through my window! Oops.<br><br>So me and this 436-page book just spent a long night together and I feel a little frazzled and emotional - is this what they call <u>book withdrawal symptoms?</u> No, you're right, it's probably called sleep deprivation, but regardless! I somehow got sucked into this subterranean troll fantasy world and I wasn't coming out for no one. This is one of those books that I'd been putting off because of the length, but it seemed to fly by in a flurry of magic, romance and troll villains. I blinked and it was over. So sad. <b>Where's that bloody sequel?</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395499072i/9007455._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><u>So... trolls. Perhaps not what you were expecting.</u><br><br><b>Myth #1: Trolls are ugly.</b> Nuh-uh. Not all of them anyway. That's the thing about trolls that makes them so deadly... it's real easy to be seduced by their beautiful faces and twinkly grey eyes. They catch you off guard. No one expects those kind of exteriors to hide something twisted, callous and sadistic on the inside. How will Cecile ever know who can be trusted when the monsters wear such pretty disguises?<br><br><b>Myth #2: Trolls are stupid.</b> Not these trolls. These trolls are cunning, calculating and ruthless. They have eyes everywhere. They know what you're going to do next before you do - okay, not literally. With every one of these clever, beautiful creatures out to get Cecile, she will have to be smarter, more cunning, than she's ever had to be before.<br><br>The upshot of this story is that a young woman called Cecile is kidnapped and sold to trolls. Not only that, but she is forced to marry their prince in the hopes that she can break a centuries-old curse that seals the trolls within their subterranean mountain world. The prophecy says that a human woman with red hair and the voice of an angel will be the one to break the curse. Cecile must learn to adapt to this world as best she can, but the longer she lives without the curse being broken, the more she becomes expendable - for what use is she to the trolls if she cannot do the one thing she was brought there for? But something else is happening too. Beneath the exterior of this structured troll society, a revolution is brewing. And Cecile is about to get caught in the middle of it.<br><br><b>The setting is a dark, underground world full of danger and magic.</b> It was so easy to be pulled into this book and get lost down in the darkness under the mountain. The lack of escape and claustrophobia felt so real to me that I couldn't look away - I was almost as desperate for Cecile to escape as she was. But, as I'm sure you won't be surprised, there's more to this book than dark grittiness and unfulfilled prophecies... there's <b>friendship</b> and <b>romance</b> too. <br><br>There are a lot of complex characters in <i>Stolen Songbird</i>. Trolls are not all 100% evil because that wouldn't be half as fun. Cecile comes to learn that trolls have the same capacity for good and evil that humans do. She discovers that many are prisoners held captive by the monarchy, just as she is. And she discovers that her new husband might not be all he first seems. I especially liked how the characterization of Tristan and Anais was handled. The former starts off as a seemingly bratty, selfish individual but is gradually developed into something more well-rounded and likable. The romance between him and Cecile didn't feel forced like so many YA fantasy romances do, nor did it drain all the juice from the main plot. <br><br><b>Anais was another pleasant surprise.</b> When she was first introduced, I found myself rolling my eyes and thinking "oh, here we go again". But I was completely wrong. While she at first appears to be the beautiful but over-sexualized "other woman" and an enemy of Cecile, she is developed into something much more. She becomes multilayered and friendship begins to take shape between her and Cecile. I liked this part of the story a lot.<br><br>There is one thing that didn't really make sense to me. A lot of YA novels - fantasy, sci-fi, dystopian, whatever - portray societies in which women are second class citizens. Whether they are slaves to men or expected to fulfill a particular role, this is quite a common feature. And I suppose it poses more challenges in the story when the vast majority of protagonists are female. This is fine, I don't mind. But there appear to be some contradictions over this in <i>Stolen Songbird</i>. We are told the trolls are valued based on power, not gender - it doesn't matter whether you're male or female, but it instead matters how much magic you have. And yet, a lot of trolls appear pretty misogynistic:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“But she’s his wife,” Tristan said indignantly. “She is duty-bound to go wherever he wants her to go.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Since when? That wasn't what we were told a couple of chapters back. But these are nitpicky things that didn't ruin the book for me. Just thought I should note them. <br><br>In the end, <b>I thought this book was excellent</b>. Unputdownable, even. And the end leaves us in a perfect position: a nice balance between wrapped up and need-to-know-what-happens-next. It leaves room for a sequel that I not only want to read, but believe has the potential to be a very different kind of story to this first installment. I'm pretty damn excited!<br><br><a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/lm/#/users/10010/profile" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390671357i/8260477.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4968762233296554457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Regan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19645927-regan"><img alt="Regan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437809914p2/19645927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_1578745177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578745177" />
    <a title="Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23179211-riley"><img alt="Riley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601446413p2/23179211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578745177?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Riley" href="/user/show/23179211-riley">Riley</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578745177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7240124313286237993">WOW. wow.<br/>I loved this book! Everything about it was captivating. The characters, the world, the magic system. The plot was such a rollercoaster. I am definitely going to read the next book ASAP! </span>

<div id="review_2070939763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2070939763" />
    <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews"><img alt="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492999740p2/66199133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2070939763?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews">Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=magic-etc">magic-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=random-shit">random-shit</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=fey">fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2070939763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4175901260534604566"><b>What the fuck is it with me and trolls?!?</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508177066ra/24188420.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can say <b>without a shadow of a doubt</b> that this book is a must-read! The world building, the unique plot, the antihero love interest just all hooked me right away <br/><br/><b>Cecile </b> was an interesting perspective- not a Mary-Sue sissy but also not exactly Xena the warrior princess. I liked her character of questioning everything and POV as the weak human trying to trick the powerful trolls...but tbh finishing the book, nothing about her character really stuck out at</span>
  <span id="freeText4175901260534604566" style="display:none"><b>What the fuck is it with me and trolls?!?</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508177066ra/24188420.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can say <b>without a shadow of a doubt</b> that this book is a must-read! The world building, the unique plot, the antihero love interest just all hooked me right away <br><br><b>Cecile </b> was an interesting perspective- not a Mary-Sue sissy but also not exactly Xena the warrior princess. I liked her character of questioning everything and POV as the weak human trying to trick the powerful trolls...but tbh finishing the book, nothing about her character really stuck out at me as being unique to only her <br><br>she wasn't exceptionally brave. she wasn't very sassy. she wasn't snarky. she was just there taking everything in <br><br>The writing went for short and shocking which worked really well with Cecile's POV of everything being new and dangerous that I was immediately thrown into this world <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"The girl rose, and her eyes laches onto me. She was beautiful, for an instant, and then her expression twisted with rage." </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Like damnnnn girl you got kidnapped and the other bitch is mad, what a world <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455737497ra/18144482.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456262426ra/18212004.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Mac</b> was the cool best friend that lost his lady love, which meant no love triangle but i low key liked him better than Tristan the asshole *unofficial title but think it gonna catch on* <br><br><b>Tristan</b> the cliche smug stupid face prince that acts cold and heartless bc thats just how you survive in court when really... but really deep inside ... <b>he's just a sarcastic prick that does exactly the fuck he wants to</b>...except when it comes to Cecile *hehe wink wink nudge nudge*<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“His brow creased in a frown. “If you’re a joke, it isn’t an especially humorous one.”<br>I threw up my hands in frustration. “You are the most intolerable individual I’ve ever met.”<br>He bowed. “Why, thank you, Cécile. Always a pleasure to have one’s accomplishments recognized.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Both characters <b>trapped</b> in their circumstances and refusing to trust each other. God I love characters forced to work together, the banter is freaking hilarious. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Why is my closet full of dresses?”<br>“Are they mine?” I asked with interest.<br>Silver eyes fixed on me. “Well, they certainly are not mine. Unless you imagine that I dress up in ladies’ clothing and prance about the palace when the mood strikes me?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503284152ra/23645742.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485817896ra/21851091.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly <b>the world-building wasn't overly spectacular</b> but the idea of trolls was just so unique and intriguing. Plus the concept of being stuck underground for years and years. <b>Fuck that would suck.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He stopped, the weight of his sorrow greater than any mountain. “And if I had the choice, I never would. I love you, Cécile. I will love you until the day I take my last breath and that is the truth.” He kissed me hard. “Forgive me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Oh god now hes a maytr that just wants to protect her<b> AND IM NOT CRYING, YOURE CRYING</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490762049ra/22341352.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452213635ra/17662328.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I heard Jérôme’s voice. He was trying to soothe me, but the words meant nothing. I had to go back. Tristan was trapped. He was in danger. I had to go back.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Why is this POV so freaking well done?!? She feels a range of emotions, isn't totally selfish or selfless. You can actually feel her fear and failure and helplessness <br><br>OH FUCK A DUCK, NO NO NO NON<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b><i>“I prefer certainty to hope.” She made a face. “What makes you think you are even capable of subduing one of us? And not just any Fa…” She broke off. “Not just any troll. The most powerful troll in this world.”<br></i></b>Oh you little fucker, they aren't actually trolls. They are just iron poisoned faires. There goes the one unique thing about this book AND ITS BACK TO THE CLICHE. Dang trolls was all new and interesting compared to basic fey shit <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b>And OFFFF COURSEEE the book ends on a cliffhanger</b> that leaves you screaming and wanting to know what the fuck happened to Tristan like is he okay or what, can I help him, what exactly is Cecile doing to help this situation, <b>and maybe he should just leave her for me.</b>...just saying... <br><br>Overall an extremely entertaining read but hoping for some more character development/uniqueness to further distant it from other cliche books.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2284948656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2284948656" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2284948656?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781735988238" href="/book/show/55787191-stolen-songbird">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=faeries-elves">faeries-elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=wish-list">wish-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2284948656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16329771040431899099"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495752527ra/22853382.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <br/>
  <i>“I cringed, though; for as much as I did not want to marry a troll, I was just as certain the troll didn’t want to marry me.”</i>
  <br/>
</blockquote><br/>Now, <i>THIS</i> was an <b>unputdownable book</b>! Whoo! If I hadn’t begun this the night before my first day of the autumn term, I would’ve, <i>without a doubt</i>, finished this in one sitting. Having said that, I did read this during <i>every spare moment</i> in between my classes. Thus, I was already a quarter of the way through <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21851568.Hidden_Huntress__The_Malediction_Trilogy___2_' title='Hidden Huntress (The Malediction Trilogy, #2) by Danielle L. Jensen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hidden Huntress</a> (aka Book #2) before I even got home! :D<br/><br/>I’</span>
  <span id="freeText16329771040431899099" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495752527ra/22853382.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <i>“I cringed, though; for as much as I did not want to marry a troll, I was just as certain the troll didn’t want to marry me.”</i>
  <br>
</blockquote><br>Now, <i>THIS</i> was an <b>unputdownable book</b>! Whoo! If I hadn’t begun this the night before my first day of the autumn term, I would’ve, <i>without a doubt</i>, finished this in one sitting. Having said that, I did read this during <i>every spare moment</i> in between my classes. Thus, I was already a quarter of the way through <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21851568.Hidden_Huntress__The_Malediction_Trilogy___2_" title="Hidden Huntress (The Malediction Trilogy, #2) by Danielle L. Jensen" rel="nofollow noopener">Hidden Huntress</a> (aka Book #2) before I even got home! :D<br><br>I’m astounded that this novel was <b>over 450 pages</b>, considering what a <i>fast read</i> that it was! And, props to you people, who had to wait in anticipation for the future books of this trilogy! The binger in me is in awe of your dedication and patience (*cue round of applause*)! &lt;3 <br><br>So…I had no expectations going into this, because I’d <i>never</i> seen anyone reading this, either on Goodreads or in my daily life. This book is basically combination of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20830060.La_Belle_et_la_B_te" title="La Belle et la Bête by Gabrielle-Suzanne Barbot de Villeneuve" rel="nofollow noopener">La Belle et la Bête</a> (aka Beauty and the Beast) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/183660.Fairest" title="Fairest by Gail Carson Levine" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> (a girl who isn’t beautiful in looks, but has a beautiful voice instead), with <b>trolls</b>. Also, the French speaker (or learner, rather) in me was delighted to see the inclusion of French names and words throughout the novel, making my immediate comparisons to <i>La Belle et la Bête</i> more authentic. &lt;3 <br><br>The<b> trolls</b> in this novel are not the ugly and stupid creatures that we know from myth, having seen them more recently in <i>Harry Potter</i> or on <i>BBC Merlin</i>. No, the trolls here are <b>powerful, strong, clever, and ruthless</b> beings. In fact, these trolls have magical abilities, cannot lie – although they can twist the truth into a deception –, have a unearthly appearances, are resistant to iron, have a separate King and Queen who rule the Summer and Winter Courts respectively, and can be controlled by their “true names.” Hmmm…does this <i>remind you</i> of any creatures that we’ve seen before in other novels? Methinks so! &lt;3 I assume that we’ll see this lore come into play in the future novels. <br><br> As for the plot, <b>Cécile de Troyes</b> is an aspiring opera singer, who is <i>kidnapped</i> by a former-friend and <i>sold</i> to the trolls who live under a mountain for gold. She is then forced to <i>bond</i> with <b>Prince Tristan de Montigny</b> to fulfil a <i>prophecy</i> to break a centuries-old <i>curse</i> cast upon the trolls, which has deprived them from ever stepping foot into the human realm again. Whilst there, Cécile gets caught up in a <i>revolution</i> brewing between the trolls in servitude and the trolls in the aristocracy. She is also simultaneously trying to prove her usefulness, as the <b>King of Trollus</b> becomes impatient for her and his son’s union to free the trolls from the cold and the dark that he’s grown tired of. <br><br>I loved <i>the multi-layered friendships, the gradual (and ADORABLE) romance, and the captivating plot</i> in this novel. If this is indeed a début novel, it was <b>exceptionally done</b>. I could not put this book down for the life of me! I was even annoyed at my professors because they were <i>getting in the way</i> of my reading time! ;) <br><br><b>Tristan</b>, although a flawed, untrusting, and inherently deceptive individual, was also sarcastic, clever, wilful, protective, brave, sexy, charming, and selfless. What more could you want for in a Prince?! Man, did he make me <i>swoon</i>!!! &lt;3<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518675423ra/25063001.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Céline</b> was a <i>fabulous</i> heroine, who managed to be very relatable, as her personality was well-balanced with bravery and humour. She is steadfast in her decision-making, makes realistic choices, and is very quick-witted, making her a wonderful character to read about.<br><br>Thus, I can <i>happily recommend</i> this book to all of you <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> fans and to those who enjoy faerie novels! Now, if you’ll excuse me, I need to finish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21851568.Hidden_Huntress__The_Malediction_Trilogy___2_" title="Hidden Huntress (The Malediction Trilogy, #2) by Danielle L. Jensen" rel="nofollow noopener">Hidden Huntress</a>! ;)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1535036619ra/26184462.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16329771040431899099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2284948656">

<div id="review_1353641023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353641023" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353641023?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353641023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14760546717403948586"><b>2.5<br/><br/>"Why can’t you believe me? Why don’t you trust me?"<br/>"Because you’re human, Cécile. You can lie, even to yourself."</b> <br/><br/>•<b>The first two hundred pages swept me off my feet</b>. I was entranced, completely bewitched. The story does not stand out for its originality, maybe -basically, we're talking about a retelling of <i>The Beauty and the Beast</i>, plus trolls- but with such a <b>flowing writing style</b> and <b>compelling plot</b>, it's extremely easy for the reader to let go of any higher expectations he might have had an</span>
  <span id="freeText14760546717403948586" style="display:none"><b>2.5<br /><br />"Why can’t you believe me? Why don’t you trust me?"<br />"Because you’re human, Cécile. You can lie, even to yourself."</b> <br /><br />•<b>The first two hundred pages swept me off my feet</b>. I was entranced, completely bewitched. The story does not stand out for its originality, maybe -basically, we're talking about a retelling of <i>The Beauty and the Beast</i>, plus trolls- but with such a <b>flowing writing style</b> and <b>compelling plot</b>, it's extremely easy for the reader to let go of any higher expectations he might have had and just enjoy what he gets. Which is pretty good, <i>more</i> than good, if, once again, not particularly unique. <br /> <br />•My main reason for loving <b>Cécile, the main character</b>, is that she's got red hair. I dyed mine red some time ago and I absolutely adore them, so yes, I'm biased. Also, she is strong, independent, strong-willed, and I deeply appreciated her lack of whining for having been torn away from her family (and if she had cried and wept her eyes out a little bit because of that, I wouldn't have minded at all because come on, she would have been completely justified). Her characterization is a bit like the book in general, that is good, but not special or unique; she doesn't really <i>stand out</i> for anything. I think that maybe, just maybe, she grows soft on Tristan slightly too fast, and her first reason for it is that he's a sight to behold. Don't get me wrong, <b>their relationship is well-developed and their romance a delicious slow burn</b>, but the very beginning made me worry indeed. <br /> <br />•As for <b>Tristan</b>, not only is he fabulously handsome, he's also devilishly clever and scheming. I'd rather the whole book were centred on his involvement in troll politics, or at least that the politics was further developed, but well, we can't have everything, and his character is charmingly <b>charismatic</b> nonetheless.<br /><br />•But then, then.... then <b>the drama came</b>, meaning the protagonists started acting like <b>freaking deranged retarded lovesick lovebirds</b>, and I'm not exaggerating. Never have I seen such a quick deterioration in a main character, let alone two. One moment they are normal, rational, with their feet firm on the ground and their heads on their shoulders, and the next they... I don't even know how to explain it. For instance, there is this gigantic disaster that totally happens because our larva of a heroine decided it was just the right moment to come out of her cocoon as a full-grown moron and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ran away because the Evil Duke told her Tristan was having an affair with another girl. So she flees and goes in the most dangerous place ever, getting herself almost killed, getting <i>Tristan</i> almost killed, getting herself almost executed on top of that  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and being generally insufferable because as I see it, being upset is not an excuse for being impulsive to the point of willingly throwing yourself in your death's way and almost killing another person in the process. No. Just no. I can't.<br /><b>This makes me so mad</b>. <br /><br />•As if that were not enough, the previously delicious scheming <b>Tristan is also abandoned by his wits</b> as soon as love blooms. So he just start a riot in his city, because it suddenly sounds like a good idea. <br />P-l-e-a-s-e. <br /><br />➽ All in all, <i>Stolen Songbird</i> is an <b>average yet pleasantly entertaining</b> read. I wanted to pull my hair out throughout the second half, but it was bearable after all. And even if I admit it's not one of my priority at the moment, I think I'm going to continue the series because the universe just <i>cannot</i> be that cruel. <br />(Or can it?)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14760546717403948586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_950821087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950821087" />
    <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic"><img alt="Irena BookDustMagic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362943196p2/17737927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950821087?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irena BookDustMagic" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic">Irena BookDustMagic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic?shelf=2014-paranormal-and-fantasy-challen">2014-paranormal-and-fantasy-challen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950821087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer777816489109688664">I just found a new favorite book series of mine. Everything that I like in a book, this book has it. And it is killing me that I will have to wait until March for it's sequel but it will be so worth it!<br/><br/>When I say everything, I mean everything: I was laughing, I was swooning, I was nervous, stressed, holding my breath while reading it, releasing it out loud... I liked, I loved, I hated, I was even yelling in my mind at some of the characters...<br/><br/>I have to accentuate that this book left me wondering</span>
  <span id="freeText777816489109688664" style="display:none">I just found a new favorite book series of mine. Everything that I like in a book, this book has it. And it is killing me that I will have to wait until March for it's sequel but it will be so worth it!<br /><br />When I say everything, I mean everything: I was laughing, I was swooning, I was nervous, stressed, holding my breath while reading it, releasing it out loud... I liked, I loved, I hated, I was even yelling in my mind at some of the characters...<br /><br />I have to accentuate that this book left me wondering about all of the directions this story could develop and I really don't know how I'm gonna stick it out not knowing it until March. I'll just have to. But seriously, if it was released yesterday, it would be the only way I would be okay with.<br /><br />Let's talk about the characters. The main Character, Cecile; is a kick-ass redhead who is likeable and smart most of the time, but at times she can make some stupid decisions and I can honestly say at time I was afraid of all the wrong directions her decisions could lead us. Wrong for her, other characters and the world itself.<br /><br />Then there is Tristan. Likeable most of the time but he seemed kind of lost and trough the whole book I can't say I trusted him completely. I still don't. There are 2 more books that need to be released and a lot could happened. <br /><br />Tristan's father, the King, I didn't like. But there are some side characters that are worse and I hated them!<br /><br />There are some that don't have a big part in this story, they are side characters but I can see they could became more important, if not maybe the key for the story develop in other books. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Tristan's brother and Chris  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The book is written in two POVs. Cecile's for the most of the book and Tristan's at some chapters. I think the writer did a great job by doing it because it had to be done that way so we could know some things Cecile didn't know, but it still didn't show us everything so we still had to question some things.<br /><br />All in all, if you like fantasy, specially faerie stories, I say give it a try. I think you will love it! I certainly did!</span>
  <a data-text-id="777816489109688664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_890132397" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890132397" />
    <a title="Brandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi"><img alt="Brandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431565587p2/4765786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/890132397?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandi" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi">Brandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Ugh.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer890132397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8825367416387182283"><blockquote>
  <a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <br/>
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book started out really good- the heroine was exactly what I like: capable, fierce, intelligent, and autonomous. I loved every single bit… till she was bonded to Tristan. Also, just a side note, but I would <i>not</i> compare this to Seraphina. I haven’t read that one again in some time, but it was much better imo, and Graceling was a complete DNF for me. So I suppose I shouldn’t have hoped that this one was going to fare better on my personal enjoyment meter. I’m such a sucker th</span>
  <span id="freeText8825367416387182283" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <br>
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br><br>This book started out really good- the heroine was exactly what I like: capable, fierce, intelligent, and autonomous. I loved every single bit… till she was bonded to Tristan. Also, just a side note, but I would <i>not</i> compare this to Seraphina. I haven’t read that one again in some time, but it was much better imo, and Graceling was a complete DNF for me. So I suppose I shouldn’t have hoped that this one was going to fare better on my personal enjoyment meter. I’m such a sucker though, I always want to <b>believe</b>, lol.<br><br>So here we have our girl who is painfully and brutally abducted away to a place that heretofore was nothing more than a myth. Trollus. Turns out that trolls are real, not all of them are the hideous under-the-bridge types, and some are startlingly beautiful. Such was the case in Prince Tristan and I saw that his pretty face seemed to have more effect on Cecile than I liked. Sure, she drank the magic potion that bonded the two of them so that each others emotions were always in the others head, and that most certainly would have fostered some softening of feelings, but it was too much for me. <br><br>Tristan is embroiled in the political entanglements that rule Trollus and there is a divide between the trolls who want free of their curse and those who want to keep all troll lines pure bloods. Tristan, being the most powerful of all, and being bonded to a human, wants to make sure nobody can use her against him but fails miserably- and it was the stupidest thing ever. Cecile goes about her life slowly but surely being less and less amazing as she started out, but still tolerable, and then suddenly she realizes that she loves her husband. Out of the blue. They didn’t sleep together (I mean sleep not sex), they never spent time together, the only time they <i>did</i> spend with each other was spent in fostering an image of a troll-hating-human affiliation. Cecile was able to know that Tristan wasn’t as horrible as he was acting thanks to being aware of his emotions in the back of her mind. But then one day their arch nemesis plays the jealousy card on her and she falls for it <b>so hard</b> that nearly everything was ruined and she almost died. This jealousy aspect didn’t abate for so long that I was about to pull my hair out and I still hate it- it’s not the girl I met in the beginning, and it was so stupid since she had nothing to base her love on. And the whole thing was just UGH. And furthermore- the troll that was used in this instrument of jealousy wasn’t even a bad guy <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she was hopelessly in love with Tristan, yes, but she was also one of his closest friends and she was NOT horrible. She even told Cecile how she looked pretty in yellow, she made sure to help her at every single turn like Tristan asked, never once saying she wouldn’t help because she knew it was important to Tristan. The whole creation of this “triangle” was really annoying for me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br> <br>To further my annoyance of the needless love shape was the fact that Cecile is suddenly in a shape with a boy from her village that comes to Trollus with his dad to trade. This was completely and totally pointless in my mind, all it served was to – <u>and I don’t exaggerate</u>, have Tristan and him <b>fight over Cecile</b>. It was so out of left field and pointless and on the heels of that jealousy fiasco that I just couldn’t. By that point I was no longer in love with the story or the characters and instead just wanted to get it over with. <br><br>The whole time that all this is going on the main theme of the story- the curse, was never even close to being resolved. That disappointed me because I knew I was running out of book to get a real solution, but I figured there’d be at least some movement… but no, not really. What did make me question the myth of the trolls was that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Cecile wakes up from her injuries at her Grandma’s the grandma knew “troll gold” just by looking at it, but yet trolls were supposed to be mythical creatures I thought. That made no sense to me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There were a few inconsistencies like that that I highlighted but I don’t want to put tons of quotes in the review. <br><br>One major detail in this story that nearly made me rage quit was when Cecile decided to single handedly take on a crazed and powerful troll… alone. I can’t even with that. She was beaten when she was abducted and never complained, but then later in the book she fell and scrapped her knee- getting a few stitches, and then continued to complain about it, but yet was totally fine standing her ground against the crazy and crazy powerful troll. The one that nearly NOBODY else would even mess with because he was so strong. This whole- just ugh. I can’t. We’re also left with a nice little cliffie and it worked because I want to know what the hell happens about this damned curse. I don’t want to keep going about how much I was let down because taking all my notes and quotes and putting it in here would take too long.<br><br>Basically I would say that this book got worse for me as time went on, but I don’t think that it’ll be that way for any other books in the series. The writing itself was good; it was nicely paced and there was some great elements in there that make me think this could definitely get better with time. I think this book will be the one that has people wanting to be forgiving enough to let go of certain things, or ones like me who can’t move past them, and just a handful in the middle. <br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8825367416387182283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_838122677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838122677" />
    <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always"><img alt="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562987681p2/5478965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838122677?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always">Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=i-am-not-pleased-with-that-cliffie">i-am-not-pleased-with-that-cliffie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=holy-shit-that-ending">holy-shit-that-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=might-make-you-shit-bricks">might-make-you-shit-bricks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=swoony-book-boys">swoony-book-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=ending-sucked">ending-sucked</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838122677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13734280527774412298">Want to read this fabulous book? <b>
  <a href='http://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/2015/01/03/a-deadly-christmas-danielle-l-jensen/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Enter the giveaway on my blog for a SIGNED copy of Stolen Songbird!</a>
</b> Open internationally!<br/><br/><a href='https://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402064697i/9889376.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Read in February 2014 | 4.5 stars<br/><br/><blockquote>"They aren't ugly. More like beautiful things that have had the misfortune of being broken."</blockquote><br/><br/><i>Stolen Songbird </i>just might be my favorite novel of the year so far (but it's only February--too early to tell), with its <strong>magical setting, beautiful writing, truthful characters and engaging story</strong>. This one definitely had some irritating moments,</span>
  <span id="freeText13734280527774412298" style="display:none">Want to read this fabulous book? <b>
  <a href="http://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/2015/01/03/a-deadly-christmas-danielle-l-jensen/" rel="nofollow noopener">Enter the giveaway on my blog for a SIGNED copy of Stolen Songbird!</a>
</b> Open internationally!<br><br><a href="https://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402064697i/9889376.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Read in February 2014 | 4.5 stars<br><br><blockquote>"They aren't ugly. More like beautiful things that have had the misfortune of being broken."</blockquote><br><br><i>Stolen Songbird </i>just might be my favorite novel of the year so far (but it's only February--too early to tell), with its <strong>magical setting, beautiful writing, truthful characters and engaging story</strong>. This one definitely had some irritating moments, but I guess my overall excitement and enjoyment lessened whatever bad things I felt toward the novel.<br><br>We begin the story with our heroine <strong>Cécile--fierce, accepting and compassionate</strong>. She showed a great sense of bravery (physically, emotionally and mentally) by accepting her fate. At the same time, she still fought for freedom, but not at the cost of hurting anyone (whether it be people she loves or doesn't even know). She also cared for the citizens of Trollus who were abused/not given what they deserved, despite them being trolls and not humans.<br><br>At the mention of Trollus and its inhabitants, I immediately think about how much <strong>I loved the setting and how authentic it was</strong>.  We are introduced to Trollus, the home of supposedly monstrous and dangerous trolls--but let me assure you, they are quite kind and accepting. That aside, I am a huge fan of high fantasy novels since they bring us to new, beautiful worlds that we didn't think could exist. <em>Stolen Songbird</em> was no exception.<strong> I loved everything from the markets, to the mining shafts, to the palace and everything in between.</strong><br><br><strong></strong>The side characters were very interesting as well! We have Marc, the kind one who's always helpful, Anaïs, who was initially a bitch but turned out to be helpful and a bit broken, and many, many others. <strong>It was nice that each character had a personality and all contributed to the overall story.</strong><br><br><blockquote>“Watch your tongue, Tristan,” the Duchesse snapped. “Ridiculous expression, that,” Tristan said. “I can't very well observe my own tongue unless I am to sit in front of a mirror, and I can't tolerate such vanity.”</blockquote><br><br>And then, of course, we have our (swoon-worthy) hero, Tristan. At first, he may come off as rude and indifferent, but <strong>once we are <em>really</em> introduced to his character, it'll be hard not to fall for him</strong>. Being next in line for the throne, you'd think that Tristan would want to follow his father's footsteps and sort of abuse his power. But no!<strong> Tristan is gentle (and hilarious) and he really cares about his people</strong>, whether or not they are poor or even if they're human.<br><br><blockquote>“I haven't given you a reason to believe I have a single romantic bone in my body.”</blockquote><br><br>But oh, you have, Tristan dearest. The romance (*cough* and <em>angst</em> *cough*) in the novel was exquisite. <strong>There was development between both characters</strong> and it was really lovely. From victim and captor, to friends, to lovers. I couldn't help but melt a little every time Tristan showed concern or did sweet things--it's making me feel bad that I'm spending Valentine's all alone, lol!<br><br> Truly, I would recommend this one to anyone looking for a good high fantasy that'll give you <strong>all. The. Feels</strong>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13734280527774412298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/834585994?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=smart-heroine">smart-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=arranged-marriages">arranged-marriages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=unfinished-series-to-be-reading">unfinished-series-to-be-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=trolls">trolls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=most-promising-new-series-of-2014">most-promising-new-series-of-2014</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer834585994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1420468372827859717">Stolen Songbird by Danielle L. Jensen<br/><br/><b>4 ''I just fell in love'' stars</b><br/><br/><br/>The MC, Cécile de Troyes, is the daughter of a singer. The day before she was supposed to join her mother in the purpose of starting her staining to become a professional singer like her, she was unsuspectingly kidnapped and brought to Trollus, the buried kingdom of trolls.<br/><br/>Oh, I loved Cécile. I felt like I could connect with her somehow. She’s kind, strong, intelligent, honest and brave. She’s also a very gifted singer but was a</span>
  <span id="freeText1420468372827859717" style="display:none">Stolen Songbird by Danielle L. Jensen<br><br><b>4 ''I just fell in love'' stars</b><br><br><br>The MC, Cécile de Troyes, is the daughter of a singer. The day before she was supposed to join her mother in the purpose of starting her staining to become a professional singer like her, she was unsuspectingly kidnapped and brought to Trollus, the buried kingdom of trolls.<br><br>Oh, I loved Cécile. I felt like I could connect with her somehow. She’s kind, strong, intelligent, honest and brave. She’s also a very gifted singer but was always acting modest about it, which relieved me. I don’t really like when an author tries too much to make us love a character by bringing out all their talents and achievements. Also, when it came to the seventeen years old troll prince, Tristan, she was never afraid to tell him what she really thinks and contradicted him quite often. She was one of the rare persons to do so. I was like <i>you go girl! </i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396889826ra/9199003.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was an insta-love between Tristan and me. Yes, he was often acting like a spoiled rich and handsome boy but he was also charismatic, making me laugh, smile...Trolls weren’t really my cup of tea before <i>this</i> happened, so I was a little bit reluctant before picking this up. Because of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/161887.East" title="East by Edith Pattou" rel="nofollow noopener">East</a> (which I enjoyed and recommend by the way), I made myself quite an opinion on those creatures. Basically, I started to hate them. But…the characters of Stolen Songbird succeeded to change my perspective on trolls and what I knew of them. <br><br>The writing is fabulous, very well done! The world Danielle L. Jensen created is admirable, interesting and well built. The descriptions are never too long or boring, shaped perfectly to the situations, actions. They actually bring to life many characters (even the smallest ones) and majestic places. The plot is captivating and the book in itself is quite amazing. <u>I easily classed this new series in my most-promising-new-series-of-2014 shelf.</u><br><br>Enjoy!<br><br>P.-S.: I would like to have the book two please, like now…^ ^<br><br>Pretty please?<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396889826ra/9199004.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1420468372827859717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/735419245?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer735419245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16596551247356087650">Originally Read 6/17/14<br/>REREAD: 6/5/15<br/><br/>Original Review found at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com'>www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>Wow..what a story! what superb writing! what an amazing...EVERYTHING! I LOVED IT! A MUST OWN!<br/><br/>The world building was incredible, I felt like I had actually transported to the world of Trollus and walked side-by-side with these characters. The setting was magical and I was sucked in by page 5. The plot was interesting, complex yet it flowed and had good pace. There was mystery, adventure, romance, action</span>
  <span id="freeText16596551247356087650" style="display:none">Originally Read 6/17/14<br />REREAD: 6/5/15<br /><br />Original Review found at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com">www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com</a><br /><br />Wow..what a story! what superb writing! what an amazing...EVERYTHING! I LOVED IT! A MUST OWN!<br /><br />The world building was incredible, I felt like I had actually transported to the world of Trollus and walked side-by-side with these characters. The setting was magical and I was sucked in by page 5. The plot was interesting, complex yet it flowed and had good pace. There was mystery, adventure, romance, action, everything that makes an amazing story. <br /><br />A heroine who's not whiny but who is capable, fierce, believable, and intelligent! Yet she has her faulty moments like we all do which makes her human and relate-able. Cecile is the key to this whole story. A girl literally stolen/kidnapped from her life and taken to the caves of the trolls and is forced to marry the troll prince in order to break the spell/curse brought upon the troll kingdom by a witch, which forces the trolls to NEVER leave their cave kingdom. <br /> <br />Tristan-a swoon-worthy male lead who is everything I love in a male character. Smart, aggressive, passionate, sarcastic and kind. He is the good leader this kingdom needs in order to survive and not repeat the past that made the witch curse them and their kingdom. Yet he has to play his role to his father as the prince and future heir to the kingdom.<br /><br /><br />The overall story and idea of trolls as new and different and I loved every minute of my time reading this story. Some trolls are hideous and others are not, the workings of the troll kingdom was unique. The side characters were even worth reading about, and who contribute to the plot development. They were not just there to provide a counterpoint to the story and that is what makes this whole story so great. The romance didn't overwhelm the story but had a nice pace to it and the fact that Tristan and Cecile hate each other for a good portion of the story was GREAT it added conflict to the characters story themselves which I love. <br /><br />Overall I loved this story it was everything I enjoy in story so I will own this in hard copy!<br /><br />Sexual Content: mild (some kissing)<br />Language: moderate (PG)<br />Violence: moderate<br />Drugs/Alcohol: mild/none</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11568681032253732680"><b> Full Review </b><br/><br/>I think this was my first book with trolls and i was not disappointed !!<br/><br/>I went into this book without knowing anything (I probably read the synopsis in the past but I forgot everything I read lol) so it was an interesting ride.<br/><br/><b> What I liked </b><br/>- I liked the premise in general.   <span id="freeText11568681032253732680" style="display:none"><b> Full Review </b><br /><br />I think this was my first book with trolls and i was not disappointed !!<br /><br />I went into this book without knowing anything (I probably read the synopsis in the past but I forgot everything I read lol) so it was an interesting ride.<br /><br /><b> What I liked </b><br />- I liked the premise in general. About a human who somehow finds herself in troll land with no escape and is bound to one of them. She learns that she is the key to breaking a curse that has plagued the land for centuries. She then realizes that not all of them are as bad as she thought and now she's conflicted between staying to help them and escaping. <br /><br />- There are a few tropes I like and this book had two of them! The first is 'enemy-to-lover' and the second is 'bonding of characters'. I love when two characters are bonded! (they can feel each other's emotions, if one dies, it affects the other, etc) Mix that in with people who go from disliking each other to loving each other and you have a winner!! <br /><br />- I liked reading about the different types of physical appearance of trolls! A few of them look human but alot of them have some sort of deformity. <br /><br /><b>Why isnt this a 5-star? </b><br /><br />idk I just felt like something was missing. Like I enjoyed it but it wasn't something that was spectacular. <br /></span>

<div id="review_1671782756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1671782756" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,
