        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1671782756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13640136100985102270">I put this book off for quite a long time based off the description. Seriously- a book about trolls? Ehhh. I was hesitant. <br/><br/>I'm glad I listened to friends and read this anyway. It was everything I could want from a fantasy. Such a pleasant surprise!<br/><br/>So first off, <b>not all the trolls are ugly</b>. In fact.. several are beautiful. From their descriptions, they sound a bit more like fae (which its possible they are as Tristan mentions Cecile doesn't truly know what they are.) Who knows. <b>The important thin</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13640136100985102270" style="display:none">I put this book off for quite a long time based off the description. Seriously- a book about trolls? Ehhh. I was hesitant. <br /><br />I'm glad I listened to friends and read this anyway. It was everything I could want from a fantasy. Such a pleasant surprise!<br /><br />So first off, <b>not all the trolls are ugly</b>. In fact.. several are beautiful. From their descriptions, they sound a bit more like fae (which its possible they are as Tristan mentions Cecile doesn't truly know what they are.) Who knows. <b>The important thing to take away from this paragraph is that there is a troll prince and he is badass, snarky, brooding, and most certainly not ugly. </b><br /><br />The story, in short, starts off fairly fast paced as Cecile is abducted and taken to Trollus, a spelled city under the mountain where trolls live (and can't leave via a magical curse.) She's said to be the one to break said curse by marriage to the troll prince (Tristan.) Of course, nothing is that easy- and things under the mountain grow complex as Cecile realizes Tristan isn't what he seems and there is much more to Trollus than meets the eye. <br /><br />Overall, this was a lot of fun. The pacing was perfect and the story kept me quite entranced. I definitely had some feels. My only complaint is that Cecile seemed to resign to her fate fairly easily. She wasn't bad for a heroine and she had some great moments.. <br /><br />The world building was pretty cool although some of the magic (especially the bond) seemed to flip flop on the actual rules. It could be that I just misunderstood it but there were quite a few times where the rules that were set "conveniently" didn't apply to the circumstances.<br /><br />I recommend this as a general fantasy. The whole arranged marriage in books has really let me down lately- but this one was refreshing and unique. It is worth the read.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/herbookishthings/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14646382059648530392">I would definitely reread in a heartbeat.<br/><br/>Oh, and let me just say Tristan fulfills my sarcastic, hot bad boy quota:<br/><br/><b>“You look ridiculous walking around the city carrying an empty wineglass.   <span id="freeText14646382059648530392" style="display:none">I would definitely reread in a heartbeat.<br /><br />Oh, and let me just say Tristan fulfills my sarcastic, hot bad boy quota:<br /><br /><b>“You look ridiculous walking around the city carrying an empty wineglass. I don't care to be associated with a drunk. Particularly one who damages glassware.”</b><br /><br />I loved the general plot line: trolls, girl kidnapped against her will and forced to marry hot bad boy prince, political intrigue, and magic. I think my favorite thing besides Tristan was the setting –I loved that it was so different, it reminded me of the caves in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1656001.The_Host__The_Host___1_" title="The Host (The Host, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Host</a>.<br /><br />I will say I didn’t know where this plot was going. I thought I did but it took a different direction and while that is wonderful for lots of people, I was disappointed. I felt the ending action was a bit lackluster –things happened, but they all just felt really small &amp; I don’t know, I was expecting something really epic because of the awesome premise. Still, I will definitely be reading the sequel because there were lots of plot lines unanswered and a big cliffhanger, plus the world of Trollus is so fascinating in itself &amp; I love all of Tristan &amp; Cecile’s dialogue &lt;3 <br /></span>

<div id="review_862610586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/862610586" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/862610586?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=you-call-that-an-ending">you-call-that-an-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=kinda-steamy">kinda-steamy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer862610586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6913165057357044357">After trudging through a glut of mediocre Young Adult fantasies (probably including too many self-published ones), this one hit me, at the time I first read it, like a ton of bricks. I was all, YES! layered personalities! Complex motivations! Non-TSTL (Too Stupid to Live) heroine! 5 stars!!<br/><br/>Looking at this novel again, with the benefit of some hindsight, I'm thinking that maybe I had just read too many self-published and freebie paranormal/fantasy romances on my Kindle and it skewed my views. Thi</span>
  <span id="freeText6913165057357044357" style="display:none">After trudging through a glut of mediocre Young Adult fantasies (probably including too many self-published ones), this one hit me, at the time I first read it, like a ton of bricks. I was all, YES! layered personalities! Complex motivations! Non-TSTL (Too Stupid to Live) heroine! 5 stars!!<br /><br />Looking at this novel again, with the benefit of some hindsight, I'm thinking that maybe I had just read too many self-published and freebie paranormal/fantasy romances on my Kindle and it skewed my views. This is a pretty good book; a lot of readers (especially the ones who like romantic YA fantasy) will love it. But it has its issues, like many (most) paranormal romances.<br /><br /><i>Stolen Songbird</i> is the story of a young woman, Cécile, who is taken by trolls into their underground kingdom and forced to marry the troll prince. Luckily for Cecile, these are handsome trolls (who knew there was such a thing?), not the stuff of nightmares.<br /> <br />The trolls do have distinct personalities and hidden layers instead of being one-dimensional cardboard characters, all good or all evil. They have hidden motives that only gradually become apparent. Their history is painful and mysterious and probably (it remains to be seen, in the sequels, of course) other-worldly. <br /><br />Cécile makes some rash and impulsive decisions along the way. That thing I said about her not being TSTL? I kind of take it back. But at least for the most part I could understand and sympathize with why she did what she did, and I thought that on some level it made sense.<br /><br />The romance is a pretty standard PNR romance. It manages to hit several romance tropes, but if you love that sort of thing anyway, I thought this was pretty well done. <br /><br />"Malediction" means "a magical word or phrase uttered with the intention of bringing about evil or destruction; a curse." The main curse in this book is the one that keeps the trolls locked in their underground kingdom but, like most things in this book, it looks like there's more to it than meets the eye.<br /><br />If you like YA fantasies with a strong romantic element, this is a solid one. But I still like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/142776.The_Hollow_Kingdom__The_Hollow_Kingdom_Trilogy___1_" title="The Hollow Kingdom (The Hollow Kingdom Trilogy, #1) by Clare B. Dunkle" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hollow Kingdom</a> better, another stolen bride book with a great young woman protagonist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6913165057357044357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I'm obsessed with <i>Labyrinth</i>, so when I see a romance cross my path that promises to woo me with similar tales of faeries, goblins, elves, or trolls, I obviously get more excited than a kid on his or her birthday. When the <i>Malediction </i>trilogy went on sale for Kindle a few years ago, I bought every single book, because there was NO WAY, my eternal optimist said, NO WAY this wouldn't be good. My eternal optimist can be an eternal idiot and </span>
  <span id="freeText10394494726287957908" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I'm obsessed with <i>Labyrinth</i>, so when I see a romance cross my path that promises to woo me with similar tales of faeries, goblins, elves, or trolls, I obviously get more excited than a kid on his or her birthday. When the <i>Malediction </i>trilogy went on sale for Kindle a few years ago, I bought every single book, because there was NO WAY, my eternal optimist said, NO WAY this wouldn't be good. My eternal optimist can be an eternal idiot and is responsible for 99.9% of my stupid book-buying decisions, but luckily for me, this particular decision was 100% <i>spot-on</i>.<br><br><br><br>Cecile is a talented singer who lives in a village with her father and brother. While on her way to go to her mother in the nearby city, to sing on stage, she is kidnapped by a man who has decided to deliver her to the trolls imprisoned in their kingdom under a mountain in exchange for Cecile's weight in goblin gold. Once in the kingdom of Trollus, Cecile finds herself in a truly bizarre society filled with racism, paranoia, and power plays.<br><br><br><br>The trolls were imprisoned beneath the mountain by a witch because they were too dangerous and too  powerful to be around humans. To break the curse, they believed that they needed to marry their prince to a human woman. Despite the farcical wedding ceremony to Tristan, said prince, nothing happens, and Cecile finds herself imprisoned in a kingdom filled with bizarre people who either ignore her, threaten her, or else treat her like she's less than dirt.<br><br><br><br>Enemies-to-lovers romances are my favorites, and so are fake marriages or marriages of convenience. This book has <i>both </i>tropes and even better, it does them well. It was interesting to see how Tristan had his people's interests at heart, and how he spent every step of the way fighting his attraction to Cecile "for her own good." There's also a really rich tapestry of side characters, like Marc, Tristan's best friend who has a mismatched face, Anais, the sister of Marc's dead wife, beautiful as anything but unlikely to wed due to her flawed DNA. And then there's Tristan's evil father, his mother who has his aunt growing on her back like a sentient tumor, and so many other interesting and bizarre people, too.<br><br><br><br>This is definitely more romance-driven than fantasy-driven but the forbidden romance and the need to escape the mountain are both mired in some very good world-building. The magic system isn't really that clear, as magic is kind of a catch-all here, where trolls can do just about whatever sorts of illusions they please, but I did like the clear divide between human magic and troll magic, and based on some of the reveals in this book, I'm hoping that divide will come into play more in later books.<br><br><br><br>STOLEN SONGBIRD lives up to its hype. It's a very fun fantasy romance that's a bit reminiscent of darker stories aimed at women, like <i>Phantom of the Opera </i>or <i>Labyrinth</i>. Cinematic in scope, it's got everything from fancy dresses to a dangerous love interest, peppered with a smattering of magic.<br><br><br><br>Book two, here I come!<br><br><br><br><b>4 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10394494726287957908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1079387667" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1079387667" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1079387667?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=this-cliffhanger-killed-me">this-cliffhanger-killed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=alternative-pov">alternative-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1079387667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11738431195683618142"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426957049i/14131186._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What I loved in <i>Stolen Songbird</i> can be summed up by the sentence above. Indeed, <b>what's better than a book which shows the ability to surprise you?</b> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"I think it is our nature to believe evil always has an ugly face,” he said, ignoring my question. “Beauty is supposed to be good and kind, and to discover it otherwise is like a betrayal of trust. A violation of the nature of things."</b>
</blockquote><br/>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : Regular Trolls<br/>✔ <b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : WIN! <b>Absolutely not the ugly and stupid creatures Trolls</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11738431195683618142" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426957049i/14131186._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I loved in <i>Stolen Songbird</i> can be summed up by the sentence above. Indeed, <b>what's better than a book which shows the ability to surprise you?</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I think it is our nature to believe evil always has an ugly face,” he said, ignoring my question. “Beauty is supposed to be good and kind, and to discover it otherwise is like a betrayal of trust. A violation of the nature of things."</b>
</blockquote><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : Regular Trolls<br>✔ <b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : WIN! <b>Absolutely not the ugly and stupid creatures Trolls are known to be</b>.<br><br>Now, I know a big amount of readers were annoyed by the fact that the Trolls aren't like we could expect but come on. <i>COME ON</i>. <i>Regular Trolls?</i> They're so fucking lame and stupid. I mean, how in the world could I have been interested in the story if the Trolls were what we're told they are in other fantasy books? How? During what I love to call my "fantasy days", when the only books I read except for the classics I studied in Uni were fantasy books, I met a lot of Trolls, and let me tell you, I never <i>ever</i> felt a spark of interest toward them. Never. <b>The guys are morons big ugly creatures used as villains</b> more often than not, and damn, I grew tired of this shit. The "Special Guy" (yes, <i>guy</i>, because have you noticed that Special Girls aren't that frequent in Fantasy?) must fulfill the World Saving mission he's been asked to? He met fucking Trolls in the journey. And let's the battle begin. <i>Sigh</i>. <br><br>▶ <b>Excuse me if I prefer BY FAR the way Trolls are portrayed here</b> : clever, designed to rule the world, filled with magic, not sexist (yes, that's important), and, yes, "handsome", because it seems to be the major problem for a lot of persons. Not for me. Oh, wait. Am I the only one who think that a lack of symmetry can be completely freaky? Okay, Tristan is handsome. And I'm not complaining because let's face it : I don't ship overly beautiful male-leads but come on : a troll like I used to read about in fantasy would have been an awkward love interest, I must admit, because they are STUPID MORONS, remember. Is it bad if I hope that Tristan had more scars, though? Yeah? Well, sue me. <br><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : A conceited Troll Prince who's going to fall in love at first sight.<br>✔<b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : WIN! <b>The incarnation of what I love in male-leads, no less</b>. <br><br>Let me tell you, <b>Tristan is THE guy, as he is *take a huge breath* sarcastic, strong-minded, protective but not creepy, sexy, adorable and selfless</b>. He is Ash's material, and I'm weighing my words here. One could say that he's far too perfect, but in my opinion he's not, because he does have flaws. The thing is, his flaws are the kinds that I love. He hides the truth and doesn't give his trust easily? Thanks god he doesn't! He's a master of deception? I ship that. In life and in books, I often find myself hating when people tell stories about themselves, about the way they are, so special, little things, while their acts say otherwise. In my opinion, Tristan <i>shows</i> bravery, the real courage that is to accept to show a sick image of himself to protect those for whom he cares, as Jérôme says. Oh, and he made me laugh. And swoon. And ache. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"The one, the only, as they like to say," Tristan said affably, brushing off his coat where I'd bumped into him. <br>"Which 'they' would that be?" I asked.<br>"Oh, you know. Them." He waved a hand in the air, dismissing the question."</b>
</blockquote><br><i>Annnnd</i> I'm leaving it at this otherwise my review would only be more and more declarations of love for Tristan, and you don't want to read this, do you?<br><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : A TSTL heroine with no other purpose that falling in love<br>✔<b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : WIN! <b>A brave and funny female-lead we can relate to</b>. <br><br>▶ <b>Cécile is full of awesomeness</b>. Oh, <i>look at this</i> : C<b>é</b>cile. I still don't understand why all the names are French in this book but that cracked me up at the beginning, because what is supposed to look exotic feels just ... random to me. But then, I agreed with a friend the other day because as a fantasy reader I'm sometimes appalled by the names which are chosen, Terkana, Urkira, Putrok (I'm totally creating these), so the way they used French names here is somehow refreshing. French's exotic, guys. Or not, <i>buuuut</i> that's another story.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Oh? And what feelings, pray tell, does this represent?"<br>I lifted my chin and looked him straight in the eye.<br> "My feelings for you, dear husband."</b>
</blockquote><br>So, Cécile. <b>Let's make a little list of what I loved in her, shall we?</b><br>• Be careful, because that might astonish you, but <b>the girl has a life she doesn't want to leave behind</b>, and her opinion doesn't change when she meets the magnificent Tristan. I know, I know, how fierce of her, right? <br>• <b>She's never TSTL in my opinion</b>. I mean, yeah, she does make mistakes and knows some instant-jerk reactions, but even if I was worried and mad at some point, <i>never</i>, at any moment, wasn't I able to understand why she reacted in such way. Actually, she reminds me of Megan from <i>The Iron Fey series</i>, and although I realize that a lot of readers didn't like her, <b>I always thought that her mistakes were understandable and above that, fucking realistic</b>. Have you never react without thinking of the consequences because you were upset? Nope? Ha, if that's the case, you're far better than me in a lot of ways.<br>• <b>She's not straight-on bitchy to other women</b>, and she manages to develop girls friends. Fuck YEAH! <br>• She knows how to defend herself from sarcastic comments *rubs hands*<br><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : Instalove &amp; Instalust, if you're lucky like that.<br>✔<b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : WIN! <b>A realistic, cute and adorable romance</b>. <br><br>▶ Indeed I absolutely loved <b>how their feelings gradually increase, without the sudden trust that never fails to annoy me in several YA books</b>, nope. <i>They're bonded together?</i> Correct. <i>Do they trust each other first time they meet?</i> <b>Oh, Fuck no, because you know what? Trust must be <i>earn</i>, as in real life : how amazing is that?</b> Moreover, the "I'm going to let everybody think that I hate you" trope? I'm such a sucker for that shit! <br><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : A story focused on the main characters <br>✔<b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : WIN! <b>Interesting and well-portrayed secondary characters</b><br><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : A slow-paced, about 500 pages read<br>✔<b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : WIN! <b>Such a page-turner that you wonder how in the world it could really be 500 pages</b>.<br><br>To say that the story was captivating would be an understatement : the <b>plot is well-wrapped</b> and the ending brings just the right amount of closure and angst, making you want to read the sequel immediately. <br><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : Miscommunication driven angst <br>✘<b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : FAIL! <b>Miscommunication driven angst</b><br><br>▶ Lack of communication driven angst never fails to piss me off, and <i>Sigh</i>. There was a moment where I was both worried and mad, because while I could understand Cécile's instant-jerk reactions, I was appalled at the same time because never before she let her temper drive her actions. What? I wasn't expecting that, dammit, she didn't make me accustomed to such behavior! <br><br><i>Annnnd that's</i> where I'm feeling unfair because let's face it, if she had made me used to this kind of stupid (sorry, but it WAS stupid) behavior I wouldn't have loved her but she didn't so I did like her and then I felt stabbed in the back. Oh, well. I'm just going to accept that sometimes I'm worse than a spoiled child. <i>There</i>. <br><br>Moreover, as much as I appreciate the fact that the secondary characters were multi-layered (Anaïs included), I failed to understand some of their reactions at some point <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Marc, I'm staring at you right now <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, reactions that I found out of character. <br><br>✘<b>
  <u>What you expect</u>
</b> : Unoriginal plot and world-building<br>✘<b>
  <u>What you get</u>
</b> : <b>I can't say that the plot isn't original, it wouldn't be true</b>. However I can't deny either that the world contains many similarities with <i>The Iron fey series</i>. As it is, I can't really complain because hell, I loved this series, but I would feel dishonest if I didn't bring this issue.<br><br>• A human MC in a world ruled by magic<br>• These people can't lie, and their promises are unbreakable, because you're bonded by them<br>• A hero who isn't who he seems at first, and acts as he hates the heroine to protect her<br>• The Trolls can be wounded by iron. <br>• There is a Summer and a Winter Court. <br><br>There. The similarities ARE here. Now, did they prevent me from enjoying the story? <b>Of course not</b>. Writers always take inspiration in other works, and that's for the best, if they don't end copying another book's plot and calling it their own. <b>Here it's far from plagiary, therefore I'm completely okay with that</b>.<br><br>PS : A friend just told me that some readers thought that the Trolls here might be Fae in disguise. That's a smart theory, which would explain a lot of things. I guess we'll see :)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Correct again. Remind me to choose you for my team if we ever play charades. I like a stacked team."</b>
</blockquote><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i> <br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/annas-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11738431195683618142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer979018688" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13017263545129814647"><b>JUNE 2015</b> <i>Yep, rereading another 2015 read....I just bought the sequel and that gives me a totally legit reason to reread this so soon :)</i> <br/><b>The first time I read it, I rated it 4 stars....reading this a second time, I've realized I was wrong to do so...now its 5.</b> My first review still stands, I can't add much to it, really. <br/><br/>This book really is something else. I loved the idea of it all, and I loved the main characters, and even some of the secondary characters...<i>although, of course, some of those </i></span>
  <span id="freeText13017263545129814647" style="display:none"><b>JUNE 2015</b> <i>Yep, rereading another 2015 read....I just bought the sequel and that gives me a totally legit reason to reread this so soon :)</i> <br /><b>The first time I read it, I rated it 4 stars....reading this a second time, I've realized I was wrong to do so...now its 5.</b> My first review still stands, I can't add much to it, really. <br /><br />This book really is something else. I loved the idea of it all, and I loved the main characters, and even some of the secondary characters...<i>although, of course, some of those royally pissed me off at times.</i> <b>I love Tristan and Cecile</b> and I definitely don't regret it. There is a lot a books, that have the whole 'love/hate' thing going on, but somehow, this one is set apart. I love it! <b>I really love how this was written. I think this may be added to the "Favorites of 2015" list.</b><br /><br /><i>On to the next one! I know a lot of my friends decided it was far beneath this one, but of course, I won't pass judgement until i've read it for myself.</i><br /><br />------------<br /><br /><b>MARCH 2015</b><s>I am just going to sit here.......and cry my damn eyes out over that ending...............omg. this book.........I wasnt sure what to think of it at first....the first chapter or 2 were like....<i>"what is this nonsense....?"</i> but then I was like <i>"I need this to never freaking end".</i><br />I loved the characters. Tristan was....idk, I didnt like him the first time we met him, I thought he was an immature little boy....but he grew on me, and during his chapters you really get to understand what is going on, and his reasoning for doing and saying the stuff he does. <i>Yep. it wasn't love at first 'line' but it definitely didn't stay that way for long.</i><br />I dont have much to say, except that this was an excellent book, and I'd been wanting to read it for quite some time before I actually bought it. I am glad I did! I only regret reading it so soon because I have months to wait for the sequel that I really really really need, right this second.</s></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_928954239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/928954239" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/928954239?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=serious-cliffhanger">serious-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=pea-favorites">pea-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer928954239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5898152535794075438"><b>RE-READ!!<br/><br/>*Still 5 Wonderful Stars*</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>I was terrified. It was not like the terror of running from a wolf, always knowing you can turn and fight. It was not like the sense of drowning, where there is a chance to flee to the surface. From this darkness and this place, there was no escape. I could neither run nor hide, and no one can fight the dark. All there was left for me to do was die.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Okaaaaayyyy so.....a book about trolls? <i>Really?</i> I mean, come on. In what way could this possibly be appealing? </span>
  <span id="freeText5898152535794075438" style="display:none"><b>RE-READ!!<br><br>*Still 5 Wonderful Stars*</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>I was terrified. It was not like the terror of running from a wolf, always knowing you can turn and fight. It was not like the sense of drowning, where there is a chance to flee to the surface. From this darkness and this place, there was no escape. I could neither run nor hide, and no one can fight the dark. All there was left for me to do was die.</i>
</b><br><br>Okaaaaayyyy so.....a book about trolls? <i>Really?</i> I mean, come on. In what way could this possibly be appealing? And, even if it did appeal to my senses, how could a troll possibly be hotter than the sun our dear Cecile so desperately misses? I can't answer these questions with coherent and well thought out answers, but I can assure you of one thing: <b>Tristan. Was. <i>Hot.</i></b> This story? <b>It was <i>beyond</i> addicting.</b> Every single one of these characters had a way of getting under my skin that mirrored only my favorite stories, and that is very rarely an occurrence for me. <br><br><b>"They aren't ugly." I bit my lip, trying to find the right words. "More like beautiful things that have had the misfortune of being broken." Tristan turned his face back to me. I saw the sorrow in his eyes and felt it in my heart. "Why are you always so unhappy?" I asked.<br>"I think it is our nature to believe evil always has an ugly face," he said, ignoring my question. "Beauty is supposed to be good and kind, and to discover it otherwise is like a betrayal of trust. A violation of the nature of things."<br>"Do you think trolls are evil?" I asked.<br>"Do you?" His eyes searched mine as though he might find the answer there.<br>"No," I said. "I don't."<br>He exhaled softly, reaching up and stroking my cheek with one hand. "From your lips I can almost believe it's true."</b><br><br>It's quite simple, really...Cecile is stolen from everything she has ever known, dragged 'leagues' downward to the passed over and only rarely mentioned city of Trollus where all the Trolls are trapped because of a curse some witch cast on them a long time ago. And how might they break this curse, you ask? Well, it is foretold that if a daughter of sun (who sings) and a son of night (prince) are brought together in marriage, that the curse will be lifted. Or so they think...<br><br><b>"I wish I was not what I am." His voice was twisted with anguish. "I wish I was not who I am. I wish I had met you in different circumstances, in a place far away from here, where there is no magic, politics, and deception. Somewhere where things could be different between us. I wish I was someone else."</b><br><br>Cecile doesn't <i>want</i> to be a troll's wife and she doesn't <b>want</b> to sleep in the same bed as her newly (forced) betrothed. So she does what any good wife would do: She plots. She plots and researches and waits for her moment to escape. She waits to capitalize on the mistakes of the city around her and, most importantly, her husband. But this is probably the largest problem with her whole plan: <b>He can <i>feel</i> her.</b> Every emotion. Every flinch of pain. He can <i>feel</i> if she's becoming deceptive or if she's hiding something...but can he ever really know?<br><br><b>"That was only part of it." I barely heard him speak his voice was so quiet. "I was afraid...I am afraid of loving you, knowing that someday you will go and leave me here."</b><br><br>Trolls can't lie, but humans can. Oh sure, they can deceive. They can mislead. They can lead someone off the edge of a cliff or push them off themselves, but they can't directly <b>lie.</b> Thus making for one of the biggest problems for our romantic duo throughout the whole story. Even <b>hate at first sight</b> can lead to something when you see them for what they truly are. Forced together when neither of them wanted each other, they form a bond they never anticipated. They forged an <b>understanding.</b> They had a common thread that linked them and, ultimately, bonded them. <br><br><b>"Ha ha," Tristan snorted. "How dreadfully clever. And speaking of clever, is this to be your bid for escape?" He contemplated my clothing. "In a dressing gown and bare feet? Now tell me, if I go put on nightclothes and slippers, might I join you, or is this a solo adventure?"</b><br><br>On the outside they loathe one another. They walk through the city's streets and ignore one another until absolutely necessary and even then share minimal exchanges unless venom is spitting through their teeth. But they can't hide what's on the inside: The pain. The turmoil. The misery. The <i>longing.</i> The secret 'you aren't so bad' thoughts. No, it's all fun and games until you realize you are starting to befriend and care for the other person. And when you have enemies hidden in plain sight within the city, you can't afford to show that you're falling for her, not when your carefully planned ruse could so easily crumble-Or when she could so easily be used to bring you to your knees....we wouldn't want that...would we? <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_lt0n3i8LgP1qabhns_zps4e88cbcd.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413205596ra/11478537.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_lt0n3i8LgP1qabhns_zps4e88cbcd.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Tristan was by far my favorite character, that much was certain. But it's not often I can say I loved the female lead almost as much-Cecile was strong-willed, stubborn and she <b>made mistakes.</b> <i>Costly</i> mistakes. But because of these mistakes, we got to know both her and Tristan on a deeper level. We got to see my favorite thing about any story-I've only said about one hundred times that I love seeing a desperate male lead saving the damsel in distress in the fashion that he could lose his life in exchange-and I haven't gotten to see that in action for a long long time....not in such a dramatic fashion, anyway. In short-<b>I loved how every perilous situation was handled in this book.</b> The author didn't shy from the nasty things or the bloody things and, no, there wasn't necessarily an abundance of those either, but all in all I loved seeing it play out and the desperation and love that was brought forth in these situations. Seeing Tristan and Cecile fall for one another both warmed and broke my heart....because they can only be used as pawns against one another...did I mention I loved that?<br><br><b>Dying was an easy thing to accomplish, effortless in its agony. It was living that was hard, requiring endless toil and labor, and for all one's efforts, it could be stolen in an instant.</b><br><br>Normally I would touch on what my complaints were for the story, but I really didn't have any. Like...at all. I really enjoyed this and found it was very difficult to put down at any cost. This was everything I love in a story and then some. Very rarely do action and peril meet my standards alongside the romance within the same story. I never would have guessed that a book such as this would become an instant favorite of mine, but it has and I can't seem to find the words to explain just how great this book was. It was addicting, heartbreaking, hopeful, fun, action-packed, and sweet. I fell in love with the world and what they were trying to do-the lies, the deception-all for the greater good. I am obsessed with these characters and can't wait to see how their story continues. My only hope is that it isn't <i>too</i> long of a wait before I can see what becomes of these wonderful characters with so much to lose.<br><br><b>
  <i>"This all seems like a dream now, but like every dream, eventually you must wake."</i>
</b><br><br><br><br>*********<br><br><b>*Buddy read with my wonderful friend, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/847799110?book_show_action=false&amp;ref=ru_lihp_up_rv_2_mclk&amp;uid=1933980373" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat</a> (back in October 2014 lol)*</b> <br><br><br><br>*Sorry-my review was more factual than fun, and I hate that-but I'm so tired...and it shows.*<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer846459304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11278581311327425538">Thank you, thank you, THANK YOU book!<br/>You pushed all the right buttons.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394226708ra/8824780.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><b>Let me make you a list of all the buttons hereby pushed.</b><br/><br/>A heroine who's not whiny. Or overly concerned with her looks or all the silly fripperies with which most YA heroines are sadly affected.<br/><br/>A swoon-worthy male lead.<br/><br/>Side characters who are actually worth reading about, and who contribute to the plot development. They are not just there to provide a counterpoint to the MCs' awesomeness.<br/><br/>A peculiar alternate world, well describ</span>
  <span id="freeText11278581311327425538" style="display:none">Thank you, thank you, THANK YOU book!<br>You pushed all the right buttons.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394226708ra/8824780.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Let me make you a list of all the buttons hereby pushed.</b><br><br>A heroine who's not whiny. Or overly concerned with her looks or all the silly fripperies with which most YA heroines are sadly affected.<br><br>A swoon-worthy male lead.<br><br>Side characters who are actually worth reading about, and who contribute to the plot development. They are not just there to provide a counterpoint to the MCs' awesomeness.<br><br>A peculiar alternate world, well described but without as much as a scrap of infodump. The world building is a bit imperfect, but who cares.<br><br>A relationship that builds at the right pace, with the parties actually speaking, interacting and getting to know each other before making gooey eyes. They don't even do the gooey-eye thing.<br><br>Oh, and have I already said a swoon-worthy male lead?<br>I have to make a little room for him in my (too crowded) collection of fictional boyfriends.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394226708ra/8824781.gif" alt="5668951" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11278581311327425538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" class="user" itemprop="url" name="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" href="/user/show/52488949-lia">˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2759514853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10136296370456831564"><i> “i cannot stop the world from moving. all i can do is be prepared for when it does.” </i><br/><br/>this book has made me sooo angry, i can’t believe. this review includes a (tagged) spoiler for the plot twist or whatever it was supposed to be, so be aware if you plan on reading this but i really don’t recommend doing so.<br/><br/>let’s begin with one of the very few positive aspects. the idea was honestly great and the story had so much potential, but i was just so fucking frustrated with how underdeveloped everything</span>
  <span id="freeText10136296370456831564" style="display:none"><i> “i cannot stop the world from moving. all i can do is be prepared for when it does.” </i><br><br>this book has made me sooo angry, i can’t believe. this review includes a (tagged) spoiler for the plot twist or whatever it was supposed to be, so be aware if you plan on reading this but i really don’t recommend doing so.<br><br>let’s begin with one of the very few positive aspects. the idea was honestly great and the story had so much potential, but i was just so fucking frustrated with how underdeveloped everything was, and i’m not exaggerating when i say <i>everything</i>. the characters were super dull and had pretty much no personality whatsoever. every single person (that includes trolls and humans alike) had no significant identity and character traits. oh, except being annoying because that can be applied to all of them.<br><br>the world of trollus and trolls pretend to be so incredibly progressive because they, as opposed to the humans in this world apparently, allow girls to go to school and what not, yet <i>“she’s his wife, she is duty-bound to go wherever he wants to go”</i>??? also, they talk about politics as if it were a bad thing lmao, as if it were a thing in the far distance with no points of contact to the people and not their daily lives’ interest, what a joke. they talk about cécile and that she knows nothing about politics and, in consequence, tell her to not get involved in something she has no idea about. during all that, i was sitting here and YELLING that yes, she fucking should get involved because they treat her and talk about her as if she were a second-class person (which she probably also is to them because she’s human and not a troll, oh no!) also, while the word ‘politics’ is constantly mentioned (i should’ve counted because it was mentioned like four times on one page at some point), the book never goes into more detail about what’s actually going on and it’s not developed at all.<br><br>there was no build-up of the ‘plot twist’ whatsoever and, at one point halfway through the story, she just suddenly was like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>oh, i have powers! i guess i’m a witch now</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but uhhh that’s not how it works, if you ask me. but i might be biased because i like my stories to actually make sense and be structured well enough for the reader to understand certain plot elements.<br><br>now to another part that made me so! angry! i am not opposed to insta love if it’s done well, but the one in here was just a whole mess. cécile and tristan talk to each other like once every 50 pages or so but then, completely out of the blue, she is like <i>oh tristan, i love you and i would die for you</i> and whatever, while all he did the previous chapters was talk down to her because she can’t understand him due to her being human and suddenly he’s like <i>oh no, cécile, i don’t want you to get hurt and if you die, i die</i>. what?? <br><br>while this book was super easy to fly through in the second half, which is the second and last positive thing i have to say about it, and i kept on reading because i wanted to see how it ended, it just made me incredibly mad all the time which i’m sure you’re not even able to tell after me ranting for the past five minutes! i was so fucking frustrated and kept yelling to myself, which is also unintentionally fitting since every! character! in! this! book! is! screaming! and! almost! every! sentence! ends! with! an! exclamation! point! this is how i’ll be sleeping tonight, knowing that i won’t even bother to read the next two installments in the series. and that’s the tea for today.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509491559ra/24327266.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>

<span id="freeTextContainer2326674051562437043"><b> “Dying was an easy thing to accomplish, effortless in its agony. It was living that was hard, requiring endless toil and labor, and for all one's efforts, it could be stolen in an instant.” </b><br/><br/>Like I had mentioned, I stayed up until 3 am just to finish reading this book in one sitting. So, safe to say, I love it. <br/><br/>This book truly is a unique gem among YA Fantasy. No insta-love or love triangle, no Mary Sue or Marty Stu protagonists. The story is well-paced, with plenty of action, moments of love, f</span>
  <span id="freeText2326674051562437043" style="display:none"><b> “Dying was an easy thing to accomplish, effortless in its agony. It was living that was hard, requiring endless toil and labor, and for all one's efforts, it could be stolen in an instant.” </b><br><br>Like I had mentioned, I stayed up until 3 am just to finish reading this book in one sitting. So, safe to say, I love it. <br><br>This book truly is a unique gem among YA Fantasy. No insta-love or love triangle, no Mary Sue or Marty Stu protagonists. The story is well-paced, with plenty of action, moments of love, friendship and misunderstandings, all underscored by a revolution set to change the course of their world. <br><br><u> The Relationships </u><br><b> Tristian &amp; Cecile </b><br><i> "You are wrinkling my dresses," I said. "Zoe and Elise will waste their entire day pressing them."<br>"And then they can hang them somewhere else," he snapped.<br>"You're creating an enormous amount of unnecessary work."<br>"It is the role of the aristocracy to create work," he said, kicking the pile of gowns. "Necessary or otherwise. Without us, who knows what would happen to productivity."<br>I rolled my eyes and climbed out of bed. Catching the corner of a sheet, I set to making the bed.<br>"What are you doing?" Tristian shouted. <br>"What does it look like I'm doing?"<br>"Ladies do not make their own beds! It shows initiative, which is broadly considered unladylike!"<br>My temper rising, I whirled about. "Dear me," I shouted. "I must have forgotten that my new purpose in life is to create work." Jerking all the blankets off the bed, I threw them on the floor. The pillows followed next, and I proceeded to run around the room taking all the cushions off the chairs and tossing them about the room. The last I deliberately aim at Tristian's head. It froze midair. "You are making quite the mess of my room."<br>"Our room!" I shouted back. </i> <br><br>Not sure why not I honestly found this scene so hilarious. It was honestly one of my favorites. Especially the when Cecile shouted that it was their room. For me, it was the first step toward them realizing they'd be in this together. <br>---<br><i> "Most people would have given up a long time ago - just curled up in a corner and waited to die, but you've lived every day. I don't think I've ever met anyone so tenaciously optimistic." Carefully, as if he feared I might still swat his hand away, he reached out and brushed a slimy lock of hair away from my face. "I want you to stay Cecile, but I'm afraid staying will only bring you misery." </i><br>---<br><i> “Being around you was the sweetest torture. I wanted to touch you, hold you, kiss you. I wanted all of you.” His shoulders slumped. “But I was afraid of what would happen if I gave in my desire. If I let myself love you.” </i><br>---<br><i> “I was afraid... I am afraid of loving you, knowing that someday you will go and leave me here.” </i><br><br>The tricky thing about these two, throughout the story, is though they undoubtedly love each other for a large part of the story there is this a wall. Or line neither is willing to cross for fear of being hurt by the other. Only after they lay all their cards on the table do they fully embrace their love for each other, and it was beautiful to see that finally happen. <br><a href="http://s1326.photobucket.com/user/cincin1993/media/tumblr_inline_oms6zk5xaY1syoxxy_500_zpsysepccfi.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>I love these two. They were a slow burn, but oh so worth it. The ending had me so torn up. <br><a href="http://s1326.photobucket.com/user/cincin1993/media/tumblr_inline_o41z3zu2wT1sp32rd_500_zpsgyijigo8.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>But I know these two will pervail! <br><br>*More detailed review to come*</span>

<div id="review_1286857327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1286857327" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1286857327?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1286857327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3940345544237842117">I felt like this was a decent YA fantasy romance. It definitely had a few flaws but, for the most part, the characters were likeable and the world was a fun one. It actually reminded me a lot of A Court of Thorns and Roses but with more likeable characters and a slightly more simplistic storytelling style! <br/><br/>Cécile de Troyes is due to leave her quiet village and join her famous singer mother in the big city when she is abducted by a local village wastrel and sold to a bunch of Trolls who live unde</span>
  <span id="freeText3940345544237842117" style="display:none">I felt like this was a decent YA fantasy romance. It definitely had a few flaws but, for the most part, the characters were likeable and the world was a fun one. It actually reminded me a lot of A Court of Thorns and Roses but with more likeable characters and a slightly more simplistic storytelling style! <br /><br />Cécile de Troyes is due to leave her quiet village and join her famous singer mother in the big city when she is abducted by a local village wastrel and sold to a bunch of Trolls who live under a mountain in the area! The Trolls think they can break the curse binding them to their underground city by marrying Cécile to their prince. <br /><br />The story itself was fun enough. The troll prince, Tristan, was no more happy with the idea of marrying Cécile than she was with marrying him! His evil Troll father was the one behind the abduction plot so it made both Tristan and Cécile easy to root for. I did quite like them as a couple so that aspect of the story definitely worked for me. <br /><br />The Trolls were really just regular Fey in all but name. A few of the Troll aristocracy had deformities of one form or another but a lot of them, like Tristan, were just regular supermodel hot! They had some cool magic and the tense political situation and tension in their city created by the way the full-blood Trolls treated the humans (who they loathed but needed in order to trade for stuff like food) and the half-blood Trolls (who they enslaved and used as workhorses and servants) added an extra dimension to the story. <br /><br />The big flaw of this story for me was that it was all comfortably familiar stuff if one has already read a ton of Beauty and the Beast retellings and Fey romance stories. Which I definitely have! That said, this was still quite enjoyable despite its lack of originality. <br /><br />I did feel like the ending was a little weak but up until then the whole story had been fun and engaging. <br /><br />The only other thing I can really moan about was the way Jensen managed to ruin, Marc, who initially had been a fantastic and likeable character but as soon as the going got tough he did something I found pretty repulsive and afterwards Jensen tried to sweep the whole thing under the rug and forget about it which did not work for me. It was a pity as it ruined his character for me and until then he had been the strongest of the secondary characters. <br /><br />All in all this was a fun YA fantasy romance and I'll definitely be reading the sequel.<br /><br />Rating: 3.5 stars I'm rounding up to 4 stars as this was quite engaging. The weak ending and the Marc stuff cst the book half a star in my official rating! <br /><br />Audio Note: Most of the book was narrated by Erin Moon who read the Cécile POV's and I thought she did an good job. The other bits were read by Eric Michael Summerer, who did the few bits of the book from Tristan's POV and I feel like he was also a good narrator. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3940345544237842117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_846442870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/846442870" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/846442870?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer846442870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12645277230301602182">1.5 stars.<br/><br/>I once had high expectation for this book, yet despite all the glowing reviews on GR-- <i>Stolen Songbird</i> reads just like every other cookie cutter YA fantasy novel with plenty of done-to-death cliches:<br/><br/>(1) A cookie cutter heroine, who is supposed to be 'strong willed' and 'brave' but instead acting like a child by angering powerful foes and walking right into dangerous places despite clear warnings from everyone else. Even her talent at singing or her relationship with her family (include</span>
  <span id="freeText12645277230301602182" style="display:none">1.5 stars.<br><br>I once had high expectation for this book, yet despite all the glowing reviews on GR-- <i>Stolen Songbird</i> reads just like every other cookie cutter YA fantasy novel with plenty of done-to-death cliches:<br><br>(1) A cookie cutter heroine, who is supposed to be 'strong willed' and 'brave' but instead acting like a child by angering powerful foes and walking right into dangerous places despite clear warnings from everyone else. Even her talent at singing or her relationship with her family (included one estranged mother) is *never* being handled with any care by the author.<br><br>(2) Said heroine is kidnapped by the ugly looking trolls and is forced to marry their prince! But don't you worry! The prince just happens to be unearthly handsome, despite having a pair of deformed/bad looking parents! How convenient.<br><br>(3) Trust me...the 'romance' between the main couple is as bad as the one between Edward and Bella in <i>Twilight</i>.<br><br>(4) People praise this book for the lack of insta-love in the story, but all I can say is, finely written love-at-first-sight is still better than bad 'slow burnt' romance.<br><br>Plus, don't tell me the romance in this book isn't insta-love! The main couple have met each other for...weeks? A month? And what had they done in their time together outside of meaninglessly quarreling and mistrusting one another? Still by the end of the story they are in fucking love!? Are you kidding me?<br><br>(5) The heroine was kidnapped to the underground city of the trolls. You ask: what has she been doing in the troll's palace this whole time? Gathering up useful information? Trying to find a way to escape? Well, she gets pretty dresses, she gets to party with the noble trolls, she gets a few servants to wait on her, she fights with the troll prince whom she is forced into marrying, over the pettiest of things. *sighs*<br><br>(6) When a mean-spirited troll noble tells the heroine her 'husband' is seeing some other girl behind her back, guess how she reacts!? <br><br>...she runs right off to a maze filled with man-eating wraiths out of anger.<br><br>*facepalms*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543727986ra/26676492.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(7) This what-is-his-name handsome troll prince, didn't bother to inform the heroine what is going to happen before he binds her to him (life and mind) with magic. <br><br>I'm sorry, but being tricked into getting emotionally bound with some complete stranger without any warning really isn't the foundation of good partnership or romance, for crying out loud.<br><br>*double facepalms*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543727986ra/26676491.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(8) The world building is entirely choppy and shabby:<br><br>There is a curse (from a witch) waiting to be lifted! There are power struggle between the prince and his father! There are conflicts between the pure blood trolls and the mixed blood ones! Last but not least, there is a group of rebels hidden somewhere because, you know, you can't write a YA without some rebel groups here or there these days! But none of the elements mentioned above is ever being properly explored and developed, we are only told these things are in the story, that's it.<br><br>This book is just so bad, I won't even continue reading the sequels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12645277230301602182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_912030598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/912030598" />
    <a title="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers"><img alt="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384217885p2/14564026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/912030598?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" href="/user/show/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers">Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">ANYONE!!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=100-stars">100-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=can-t-wait-for-the-sequel">can-t-wait-for-the-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=fav-s">fav-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=i-loved-it">i-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=dual-pov">dual-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912030598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15151798073079794925"><br/>I don't even know where to begin to express my feelings on STOLEN SONGBIRD! It was so high tensed, and had my emotions in an uproar. I was screaming at times, yelling NO, you can't do that you idiot! Then I was chanting, YEAH, go for it, do it!!! This book pulled emotions out of me that I didn't even know I had! And I say that in a totally good way!!!<br/><br/><b>I absolutely, positively, undoubtedly, LOVED STOLEN SONGBIRD in every way possible!</b> <br/><br/>This book is a perfect example of the reasons why I love books.</span>
  <span id="freeText15151798073079794925" style="display:none"><br />I don't even know where to begin to express my feelings on STOLEN SONGBIRD! It was so high tensed, and had my emotions in an uproar. I was screaming at times, yelling NO, you can't do that you idiot! Then I was chanting, YEAH, go for it, do it!!! This book pulled emotions out of me that I didn't even know I had! And I say that in a totally good way!!!<br /><br /><b>I absolutely, positively, undoubtedly, LOVED STOLEN SONGBIRD in every way possible!</b> <br /><br />This book is a perfect example of the reasons why I love books. I said in my goodreads progress while I was reading this book, that "STOLEN SONGBIRD makes me remember why I love fantasy so much." And it does! I got 3 Likes from 3 different people that read STOLEN SONGBIRD that agreed with that above statement wholeheartedly. It was just sooo sooooo amazinggg!!!<br /><br />STOLEN SONGBIRD was everything I thought it wouldn't be. YEP, you read that right! I really did not NOT expect to really like this book. And I definitely did NOT expect to love it as much as I did! It felt like STOLEN SONGBIRD had magic within it's pages. Like the events that were unfolding where coming with full force, with a high power then words. I felt connected to the book and the characters. I become aware of how much I felt for these characters after tears starting running down my face and still didn't stop at the end when I closed the book. The tears only got worse! So yeah, I think it's safe to say that STOLEN SONGBIRD has left it's mark within me. It has gotten through my defenses and landed it's way into my heart! And I am SO happy it did!<br /><br />(Okay, I know I might sound like a nutball, but come on, we've all have that one (or Many) special books that just hits us full force with all its power. And that is what STOLEN SONGBIRD has done to me! ;)<br /><br /><b>THE PLOT...</b><br /><br />For five long, torturous, centuries, magical Trolls have been bound to the ruins underneath Forsaken mountain. Cursed by a vendetta of a witch, for as long as she drawls breath, the Trolls will be bound by their magical restraints that she casted on that fateful day when she uttered the spell that changed the world for both humans and Trolls.<br /><br />Trolls have looked long and far for the witch that cursed them. Sending humans out in exchange for the unlimited amounts of gold they own in search for the witch, and to find a way to break the curse the witch has doomed them all with. But every time the humans come back unsuccessful, and the Trolls have to continue to endure the punishment that their ancestor were given until their dying day!<br /><br /><b>Until... A prophecy is seen.<br /><br />"Bring forth and bound the Prince of Night and Daughter of Day and the curse will be broken." <br /><br />And their is hope in Trollus again.... <br /><br />But at what cost?</b> <br /><br />Cécile becomes the Trolls only salvation. Their only hope they have to break the curse. They believe her to be the one to free them all from their magic restraints. One way or another... she will help!<br /><br />Cécile is kidnapped and brought to Trollus and sold to the king in exchange for their gold. Cécile is strong, she's a fighter, and she's not going down without a fight. She will not roll over and do nothing. That is until the Troll prince Tristan comes into her life and changes everything she once thought about Trollus and their people. Then she meets other Trolls like the prince, and she starts to second guess who is really the good guys and who our the bad guys in Trollus. But not everyone in Trollus is capable of goodness and is willing to help others. Their is a rebellion within Trollus, some of the half-bloods (Half Troll &amp; Half-Human) want to be treated equal. They are tired of being used and abused by the full-bloods. War is on the horizon, and Cécile will have to decide where her loyalties lie, and just how far she is willing to go to help these Trolls, and if she even should!<br /><br />With Cécile's heart and mind at battle, the Troll kings cruelty and abuse to the half-bloods, her ongoing love for the Prince, being kidnapped and held by force, her new friends in Trollus counting on her to set them, and a rebellion that she just might find herself in the middle of. She has much to consider...If she makes it out, ALIVE!<br /><br />I just loved this book! And I was so MAD when I was done reading, because WOW, it ended on a serious cliff-hanger. It was TORTURE, still is. I NEED to know what's too come. And with this book just being released (at the time of this review) I will have to wait probably another whole year. A year of TORTURE!!!<br /> <br />STOLEN SONGBIRD is for any Fantasy, dystopian, paranormal, romance, action/adventure fan out there. With all these genres intertwined in one book, you would think wow, that's too many genres for one book. But nope, it's PERFECT! It had just enough of everything and was plotted just right! Danielle L. Jensen is a mastermind, and I will read anything this woman writes! Now Danielle, GIVE ME BOOK 2!!! ;)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15151798073079794925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
